Its explanations, now part of Phishnet and API CASB, can improve user decisions and SOC efficiency.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;Todayâs security ecosystem generates a staggering amount of complex telemetry. For instance, processing a single email requires analyzing sender reputation, authentication results, link behavior, infrastructure metadata, and countless other attributes. Simultaneously, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/sase/products/casb/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloud access security broker (CASB)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; engines continuously scan SaaS environments for signals that detect misconfigurations, risky access, and exposed data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But while detections have become more sophisticated, explanations have not always kept pace.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Security and IT teams are often aware when something is flagged, but they do not always know, at a glance, why. End users are asked to make real-time decisions about emails that may impact the entire organization, yet they are rarely given clear, contextual guidance in the moment that matters.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/fundamentals/reference/cloudy-ai-agent/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudy&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; changes that.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudy is our LLM-powered explanation layer, built directly into Cloudflare One. It translates complex machine learning outputs into precise, human-readable guidance for security teams and end users alike. Instead of exposing raw technical signals, Cloudy surfaces the reasoning behind a detection in a way that drives informed action.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/en-au/sase/products/email-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Email Security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, this means helping users understand why a message was flagged before they escalate it to the security operations center, or SOC. For Cloudflare CASB, it means helping administrators quickly understand the risk and remediation path for SaaS findings without having to manually assess low-level signals.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This post outlines how we are extending Cloudy across &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/email-security/settings/phish-submissions/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Phishnet&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and API CASB to improve decision making, reduce unnecessary noise, and turn complex security signals into clear, actionable insight.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;cloudy-for-email-security-users\&quot;&gt;Cloudy for Email Security users&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#cloudy-for-email-security-users\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;When an email is analyzed by &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/sase/products/email-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Email Security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, it is not evaluated by a single signal or model. Instead, a wide range of machine learning models analyze different parts of the message, from sender reputation and message structure to content, links, and behavioral patterns. This model set continues to grow as our machine learning team regularly trains and deploys new detections to keep pace with evolving threats.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Based on this analysis, messages are labeled with outcomes such as Malicious, Suspicious, Spam, Bulk, or Spoof. While these detections have been effective, we consistently heard feedback from customers that it was not always clear why a message was flagged. The decision was correct, they told us âÂ  but the reasoning behind it was often opaque to both end users and security teams.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To address this, we introduced the first version of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudy-driven-email-security-summaries/\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudy&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;u&gt;: LLM-powered summaries for detections&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. These summaries translate what our machine learning models are seeing into human readable explanations. Initially, these summaries were available in the Cloudflare dashboard to help SOC teams during investigations. Over the past few months, customer feedback has confirmed that these explanations significantly improve understanding in our detections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;As we continued speaking with customers, another challenge surfaced. Our &lt;b&gt;Phishnet&lt;/b&gt; tool allows users to submit messages to the SOC when they believe an email may be suspicious. While this empowers employees to participate in security, many SOC teams told us their queues were being flooded with submissions that turned out to be clean messages.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The result was unnecessary backlog and slower response times for emails that actually required investigation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;At the same time, customers told us that traditional security awareness training was not always enough. Users still struggled to evaluate emails in the moment, when it mattered most. They wanted more contextual guidance directly within the workflow where decisions are made.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This upgrade is designed to address both of these problems. By bringing clearer explanations and contextual education directly into Phishnet, we aim to help users make better decisions while reducing noise for SOC teams, without sacrificing security.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;the-problem-some-users-flag-too-many-emails-while-some-arent-cautious-enough\&quot;&gt;The problem: Some users flag too many emails, while some arenât cautious enough&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-problem-some-users-flag-too-many-emails-while-some-arent-cautious-enough\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;As organizations and attack techniques have evolved, so has the role of the end user. Modern email threats increasingly rely on social engineering, subtle impersonation, and psychological pressure which places users directly in the decision path.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In response, users are being asked to act as an additional layer of defense. However, traditional security awareness tools often fall short. Training is typically delivered through periodic sessions or simulated phishing campaigns, disconnected from real messages and real decisions. When users encounter an unfamiliar email, they are left without enough context to confidently assess risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This gap commonly leads to one of two outcomes. Some users submit nearly every questionable message to the SOC, creating excessive noise and slowing down investigations. Others interact with messages they should not, simply because nothing in the moment signals clear risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;By embedding Cloudy directly into Phishnet, we close this gap.Â &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Users receive immediate, contextual explanations that help them understand what Cloudflare is seeing and why a message may be risky. This enables users to make informed decisions at the point of interaction, reduces unnecessary escalations to the SOC, and allows security teams to focus on the messages that truly require attention.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over time, this approach shifts users from being a source of noise to becoming an effective part of the detection and response workflow. The result: stronger email security, without adding friction or burden to security teams.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;phishnet-for-microsoft-gets-a-cloudy-upgrade\&quot;&gt;Phishnet for Microsoft gets a Cloudy upgrade&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#phishnet-for-microsoft-gets-a-cloudy-upgrade\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;In the next month, we will be upgrading our Phishnet reporting button to extend the Cloudy summaries.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6dO9TV4MfE2R0YZ035QQ7/3693156d65a4c8aca4b2b9d57e77ce87/image1.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;882\&quot; height=\&quot;1768\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sub&gt;&lt;i&gt;The new Phishnet screens will show Cloudy summaries.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;With this upgrade, end users receive a simplified, user-friendly version of Cloudy summaries at the moment they report a message. These summaries are generated in real time using Cloudflare Workers AI and run directly on Cloudflareâs global Workers platform when a user interacts with a message in Phishnet.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When a user clicks the Phishnet reporting button, the request triggers a Workers-based workflow that aggregates structured outputs from multiple detection models associated with that message. These model outputs include signals such as sender reputation, domain and infrastructure characteristics, authentication results, link and content analysis, and behavioral indicators collected during message processing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The aggregated signals are then passed to Workers AI, where a series of purpose-built prompts generate a natural language explanation. Each prompt is designed to transform low-level detection outputs into a concise and human-readable summary. This process focuses on explanation rather than classification and does not alter the original disposition of the message.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5PSAZclxFkdcvSivalmoCn/b355e9e6cf667e6e8e9587f6946db5c6/image6.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;684\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sub&gt;&lt;i&gt;How Cloudy transforms detections into clear explanations.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For this experience, we intentionally redesigned the summaries compared to those shown to administrators in the Cloudflare dashboard. During testing, we found that admin-focused summaries often relied on technical concepts that were difficult for non-technical users to interpret. Terms such as ASNs, IP reputation, or authentication failures required translation.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To ensure end users can understand the summaries, Phishnet emphasizes plain-language explanations while preserving the meaning of the underlying detections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Signal&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;What it means&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cloudy translation for end users&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;SPF Fail&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Sender explicitly not authorized by SPF&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;This email failed a sender verification check.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DKIM Fail&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Message signature does not validate&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The message integrity check failed, which can be a sign of tampering.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DMARC Fail&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DMARC policy check failed&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The senderâs domain could not confirm this email is legitimate.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Reply to Mismatch&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Reply To differs from From&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Replies may go to a different address than the sender shown.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Domain Age&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Domain recently registered&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The sender domain is newly created, which is common in phishing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;URL Low Reputation&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Destination URL has poor reputation&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The link destination has signals associated with risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;Because this workflow runs on the Cloudflare Workers platform, summaries are generated with low latency and at global scale â so users receive immediate feedback at the moment of interaction. This real-time context allows users to better understand why an email may be risky or why it appears safe before deciding whether to escalate it to the SOC.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We are currently beta testing this experience with Microsoft customers to ensure the summaries are accurate and reliable. &lt;b&gt;Cloudy summaries are not trained on customer data.&lt;/b&gt; We are also applying additional validation to ensure the generated explanations do not hallucinate. Accuracy is critical at this stage as incorrect guidance could introduce real security risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Following the beta period, we plan to expand access to all Microsoft users. We will also bring similar upgrades to the Phishnet sidebar for Google Workspace users later in 2026.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;your-casb-findings-explained-with-cloudy\&quot;&gt;Your CASB findings, explained with Cloudy&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#your-casb-findings-explained-with-cloudy\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;But helping end users better understand what makes an email risky is only part of the story. We are also applying Cloudy to the administrative side of security operations, where clarity and speed matter just as much. Beyond Phishnet, Cloudy now translates complex CASB findings into structured explanations that help security and IT teams quickly understand risk, prioritize remediation, and take confident action across their SaaS environments.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;api-casb-in-the-wild\&quot;&gt;API CASB in the wild&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#api-casb-in-the-wild\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Inside &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/sase/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare One&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, our SASE platform, CASB connects to the SaaS and cloud tools your teams already use. By talking to providers over API, CASB gives security and IT teams:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;A consolidated view of misconfigurations, overshared files, and risky access patterns across apps like Microsoft 365, Google Workspace, Slack, Salesforce, Box, GitHub, Jira, and Confluence (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/applications/scan-apps/casb-integrations/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CASB Integrations&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Continuous scanning for new issues as users collaborate, share, and adopt new tools.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Findings that are organized, searchable, and exportable for triage and reporting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1CH5fnjMQL3oK5PdF9F1bT/d34abcaa64d536cd8706a407f20ba2a9/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1429\&quot; height=\&quot;806\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sub&gt;&lt;i&gt;A typical CASB Findings page showing detections for a Microsoft 365 finding.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;making-saas-security-straightforward\&quot;&gt;Making SaaS security straightforward&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#making-saas-security-straightforward\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Until now, understanding what exactly triggered a CASB Finding â the detections that CASB makes across connected SaaS integrations â has been a black box. While the information was there to put together an explanation of why that file, that user, that configuration was triggering a CASB Finding Type, it wasnât exactly obvious the reason why it was ultimately detected by our system.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;With the introduction of Cloudy summaries in CASB, users receive a short description of the detection rationale with the specific details of the match listed out for easy comprehension.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Unlike a simple text summary, Cloudy for CASB provides a structured breakdown designed for immediate remediation. As seen in our beta testing across different providers, from Microsoft 365 to Dropbox, the model consistently parses findings into two distinct sections:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: It identifies exactly why the finding matters. For instance, rather than just noting a &amp;#39;Suspended User,&amp;#39; Cloudy clarifies that this &amp;#39;may indicate a compromised account or a user who should no longer have access to company data&amp;#39;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: It offers immediate next steps. Instead of generic advice, it suggests specific actions, such as verifying if a suspension was intentional or reviewing an application&amp;#39;s legitimacy before revoking access.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;This structure ensures that analysts can understand the gravity of a finding without needing deep expertise in the specific SaaS application involved.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/BkfPI5VWYYaGzjjHsfyEz/16783ef841292ff66972222afda350e9/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;799\&quot; height=\&quot;867\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sub&gt;&lt;i&gt;An example Cloudy Summary in a CASB Posture Finding.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Finding Type&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Technical Signal&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cloudy Translation (Risk &amp;amp; Guidance)&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Identity &amp;amp; Access&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Dropbox:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Suspended User&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: A suspended user account may indicate a compromised account or a user who should no longer have access to company data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: Verify that the suspension is intentional and that the user&amp;#39;s access has been properly revoked.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Shadow IT&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Google Workspace:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Installed 3rd-party app&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: This installed application with Google Sign In access may pose a risk of unauthorized access to user data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: Review the application&amp;#39;s legitimacy and necessity, and consider revoking access if it is no longer needed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Email Security&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Microsoft 365:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Domain DMARC record not present&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: The absence of a DMARC record may leave the domain vulnerable to email spoofing and phishing attacks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: Configure a DMARC record for the domain to specify how to handle unauthenticated emails.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Data Loss Prevention&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Microsoft 365:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;File publicly accessible + DLP Match&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: This file being shared publicly with edit access may allow unauthorized modifications... especially given the potential sensitive content indicated by the DLP Profile match.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: Review the file&amp;#39;s content... and consider restricting access if necessary.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;We know that when it comes to our customers getting to the bottom of identified security issues, time is of the essence. We believe that any amount of unnecessary uncertainty or lack of clarity around whatâs going wrong just puts more time between an imperfect state and one that is more secure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We built this feature on the same privacy-first foundations as all products at Cloudflare. Cloudy summaries in CASB are generated using Cloudflare Workers AI, ensuring that your data remains within our secure infrastructure during analysis. The models are not trained on your SaaS data, and the summaries are generated ephemerally to aid in triage. This allows your team to leverage the speed of AI without exposing sensitive internal documents or configurations to public models.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;whats-next\&quot;&gt;Whatâs next&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#whats-next\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;For Email Security, we will continue to expand how Cloudy supports both administrators and end users. Our focus is on delivering clearer explanations, better in context guidance, and deeper integration into daily workflows.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For CASB, weâre excited to look for opportunities where Cloudy can make it even easier for CASB administrators to understand whatâs going on across their cloud and SaaS apps. Keep an eye out as we look to expand Cloudy coverage to allow administrators to query their findings using natural language, further reducing the time it takes to identify and remediate risks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Looking ahead, this includes richer explanations for additional detection types, tighter feedback loops between user actions and detections, and continued improvements to how users and SOC teams collaborate through Phishnet. Our goal is to make Cloudy a core part of how organizations understand, trust, and act on email security decisions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We provide all organizations (whether a Cloudflare customer or not) with free access to our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/email-security/retro-scan/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Retro Scan&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; tool, allowing them to use our predictive AI models to scan existing inbox messages in Microsoft 365.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Retro Scan will detect and highlight any threats found, enabling organizations to remediate them directly in their email accounts. With these insights, organizations can implement further controls, either using &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/zero-trust/products/email-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Email Security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; or their preferred solution, to prevent similar threats from reaching their inboxes in the future.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you are interested in how Cloudflare can help complex security into human action&quot;],&quot;description&quot;:[0,&quot;Cloudy is our LLM-powered explanation layer built directly into Cloudflare One. Its explanations, now part of Phishnet and API CASB, can improve user decisions and SOC efficiency.&quot;],&quot;imgPreview&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/4plooiLyILg6Jg48r5v3ke/87710382aecbbe84725ee9ad853caf5e/OG_Share_2024-2025-2026__8_.png&quot;]}],&quot;publicly_index&quot;:[0,true]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;6bn8ZofdSYZHfiOOkBl2qq&quot;],&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;From reactive to proactive: closing the phishing gap with LLMs&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;email-security-phishing-gap-llm&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;Email security is a constant arms race. Like WWII engineers reinforcing only the planes that returned, survivorship bias hides real gaps. But LLMs can help us find the invisible weaknesses.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/email-security/what-is-email-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Email security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; has always been defined by impermanence. It is a perpetual call-and-response arms race, where defenses are only as strong as the last bypass discovered and attackers iterate relentlessly for even marginal gains. Every control we deploy eventually becomes yesterdayâs solution.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;What makes this challenge especially difficult is that our biggest weaknesses are, by definition, invisible.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This problem is best illustrated by a classic example from World War II. Mathematician &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.historyofdatascience.com/abraham-wald-a-statistical-hero/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Abraham Wald&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; was tasked with helping Allied engineers decide where to reinforce bomber aircraft. Engineers initially focused on the bullet holes visible on planes returning from missions. Wald pointed out the flaw: they were reinforcing the areas where planes could already take damage and survive. The true vulnerabilities were on the planes that never came back.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1NxyKOOVeVCGbOz7hY5AFU/c382fc6186bc98fe63a7de35720f3618/image3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1536\&quot; height=\&quot;1024\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Email security faces an identical hurdle: our detection gaps are unseen. By integrating LLMs, we advance email phishing protection and move from reactive to proactive detection improvement.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The limits of reactive defense&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Traditional email security systems improve primarily through user-reported misses. For example, if we marked a spam message as clean, customers can send us the original EML to our pipelines for our analysts to analyze and update our models. This feedback loop is necessary and valuable, but it is inherently reactive. It depends on someone noticing a failure after the fact and taking the time to report it.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That means detection improvements are often driven by what attackers already succeeded at, rather than by what they are about to exploit next.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To close this gap, we need a way to systematically observe the âplanes that didnât make it back.â&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;mapping-the-threat-landscape-with-llms\&quot;&gt;Mapping the threat landscape with LLMs&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#mapping-the-threat-landscape-with-llms\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ai/what-is-large-language-model/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Large Language Models (LLMs)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; hit the mainstream market in late 2022 and early 2023, fundamentally changing how we process unstructured data. At their core, LLMs use deep learning and massive datasets to predict the next token in a sequence, allowing them to understand context and nuance. They are particularly well-suited for email security because they can read natural language and characterize complex concepts (like intent, urgency, and deception) across millions of messages.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Every day, Cloudflare processes millions of unwanted emails. Historically, it was not feasible to deeply characterize each message beyond coarse classifications. Manually mapping emails to nuanced threat vectors simply did not scale.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Now, Cloudflare has integrated LLMs into our email security tools to identify threats before they strike. By using the power of LLMs, as weâll describe below, we can finally see a clear and comprehensive picture of the evolving threat landscape.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/510saHtEz5iJRxg9Qp9zEN/8c59e619c6f6d62e8f6ced7e8f8dd401/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;888\&quot; height=\&quot;823\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Our LLM-driven categorization shows clear spikes and persistent trends across several distinct categories, including &amp;quot;PrizeNotification&amp;quot; and &amp;quot;SalesOutreach&amp;quot;.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;These LLM-generated tags provide Cloudflare analysts with high-fidelity signals in near real time. Tasks that previously required hours of manual investigation and complex querying can now be surfaced automatically, with relevant context attached. This directly increases the velocity at which we can build new targeted Machine Learning models or retrain existing ones to address emerging behaviors.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Because Cloudflare operates at global Internet scale, we can gather these insights earlier than ever before, often before a new technique becomes widely visible through customer-reported misses.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;the-sales-outreach-threat\&quot;&gt;The Sales Outreach threat&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-sales-outreach-threat\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;One of the clearest patterns weâve identified using this new intelligence is the continued persistence of malicious messages structured to look like Sales Outreach-style phishing. These emails are designed to mimic legitimate B2B communication, often presenting opportunities to purchase or receive &amp;quot;special deals&amp;quot; on unique items or services, to lure targets into clicking malicious links or providing credentials.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Once LLM categorization surfaced Sales Outreach as a dominant vector, we moved from broad visibility to targeted data collection.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Using LLM-generated tags, we began systematically isolating messages that exhibited Sales Outreach characteristics across our global dataset. This produced a continuously growing, high-precision corpus of real-world examples, including confirmed malicious messages as well as borderline cases that traditional systems struggled to classify. From this corpus, we built a dedicated training pipeline.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;First, we curated training data by grouping messages based on shared linguistic and structural traits identified by the LLMs. These traits included persuasive framing, manufactured urgency, transactional language, and subtle forms of social proof.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Next, we focused feature extraction on sentiment and intent rather than static indicators. The model learns how requests are phrased, how credibility is established, and how calls to action are embedded within otherwise normal business conversations.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finally, we trained a purpose-built sentiment analysis model optimized specifically for Sales Outreach behavior. This avoided overloading a general phishing classifier and allowed us to tune precision and recall for this threat class.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1uxwkalxVBOczIXJ1VebIs/ce1197d61c83f9756c3951d4dee77572/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1280\&quot; height=\&quot;918\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h4 id=\&quot;turning-language-into-enforcement\&quot;&gt;Turning language into enforcement&lt;/h4&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#turning-language-into-enforcement\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The output of this model is a risk score that reflects how closely a message aligns with known Sales Outreach attack patterns. That score is evaluated alongside existing signals such as sender reputation, link behavior, and historical context to determine whether a message should be blocked, quarantined, or allowed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This process is continuous. As attackers adapt their language, newly observed messages are fed back into the pipeline and used to refine the model without waiting for large volumes of user-reported misses. LLMs act as the discovery layer by surfacing new linguistic variants, while the specialized model performs fast and scalable enforcement.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is what an all-out offensive looks like in practice. It is a feedback loop where large-scale language understanding drives focused, high-precision detection. The result is earlier intervention against a threat class that thrives on subtlety, and fewer malicious sales emails reaching the inbox.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;results-of-the-undertaking\&quot;&gt;Results of the undertaking&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#results-of-the-undertaking\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The visibility unlocked by LLM-driven mapping fundamentally changed how we improve detections. Instead of waiting for attackers to succeed and relying on downstream user reports, we gained the ability to identify systemic gaps earlier and address them at the source. This shift from reactive remediation to proactive reinforcement translated directly into measurable customer impact.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The most immediate signal of success was a marked reduction in customer friction. Sales Outreachârelated phishing has historically generated a high volume of user-reported misses, largely because these messages closely resemble legitimate business communication and often evade traditional rule-based or reputation-driven systems. As our targeted models came online and were continuously refined using LLM-derived insights, fewer of these messages reached end users in the first place.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The data reflects this change clearly. Average daily Sales Outreach submissions â messages that we labeled as clean but were in fact Sales Outreach phishing emails, flagged by end users â dropped from 965 in Q3 2025 to 769 in Q4 2025, representing a &lt;b&gt;20.4% reduction in reported misses&lt;/b&gt; &lt;b&gt;in a single quarter.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7plV0JarzggZYDPHKcgmya/8762112a2c7f4c1cec70e654a1a6a4ef/image1.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1297\&quot; height=\&quot;721\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;This reduction is not just a metric improvement; it represents thousands fewer disruptive moments per day for security teams and end users alike. Each avoided submission is a phishing attempt that was stopped before it could erode trust, consume analyst time, or force a user to make a security judgment mid-workflow. We have seen this trend continue in Q1 of 2026 with average daily submissions decreasing by two-thirds.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3Y6v2oNdWrJUmXzR5igzsL/72dc19cc052185f2753adad111ce0afb/image5.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1298\&quot; height=\&quot;741\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;In effect, LLMs allowed us to âseeâ the planes that never made it back. By illuminating previously invisible failure modes, we were able to reinforce defenses precisely where attackers were concentrating their efforts. The result is a system that improves not only detection rates, but also the day-to-day experience of the people relying on it.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;the-next-front-in-the-arms-race\&quot;&gt;The next front in the arms race&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-next-front-in-the-arms-race\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Our work with LLMs is just beginning.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To stay ahead of the next evolution of attacks, we are moving toward a model of total environmental awareness by refining LLM specificity to extract forensic-level detail from every interaction. This granular mapping allows us to identify specific tactical signatures rather than relying on broad labels.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Simultaneously, we are deploying specialized machine learning models purpose-built to hunt for emerging, high-obfuscation vectors at the &amp;quot;fringes&amp;quot; that traditional defenses miss. By leveraging this real-time LLM data as a strategic compass, we can shift our human expertise away from known noise and toward the critical gaps where the next strike is likely to land.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;By illuminating the &amp;quot;planes that didn&amp;#39;t make it back,&amp;quot; we are doing more than just reacting to missed email; we are systematically narrowing the battlefield. In the email arms race, the advantage belongs to the side that can see the invisible first.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;ready-to-enhance-your-email-security\&quot;&gt;Ready to enhance your email security?&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#ready-to-enhance-your-email-security\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;We provide all organizations (whether a Cloudflare customer or not) with free access to our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/email-security/retro-scan/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Retro Scan&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; tool, allowing them to use our predictive AI models to scan existing inbox messages in Microsoft 365.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Retro Scan will detect and highlight any threats found, enabling organizations to remediate them directly in their email accounts. But LLMs can help us find the invisible weaknesses.&quot;],&quot;imgPreview&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6oHDeRmUHgxw15hsFMF6vr/69c2b8734c71b329957c188e5b5f0f91/From_reactive_to_proactive-_closing_the_phishing_gap_with_LLMs-OG.png&quot;]}],&quot;publicly_index&quot;:[0,true]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;1IAvxHyuyoZKYW249A4AvF&quot;],&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;Toxic combinations: when small signals add up to a security incident&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;toxic-combinations-security&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;Minor misconfigurations or request anomalies often seem harmless in isolation. But when these small signals converge, they can trigger a security incident known as a toxic combination. Hereâs how to spot the signs. &quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;At 3 AM, a single IP requested a login page. Harmless. But then, across several hosts and paths, the same source began appending &lt;code&gt;?debug=true&lt;/code&gt; â the sign of an attacker probing the environment to assess the technology stack and plan a breach.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Minor misconfigurations, overlooked firewall events, or request anomalies feel harmless on their own. But when these small signals converge, they can explode into security incidents known as âtoxic combinations.â These are exploits where an attacker discovers and compounds many minor issues â such as a debug flag left on a web application or an unauthenticated application path â to breach systems or exfiltrate data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflareâs network observes requests to your stack, and as a result, has the data to identify these toxic combinations as they form. In this post, weâll show you how we surface these signals from our application security data. Weâll go over the most common types of toxic combinations and the dangerous vulnerabilities they present. We will also provide details on how you can use this intelligence to identify and address weaknesses in your stack.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;how-we-define-toxic-combinations\&quot;&gt;How we define toxic combinations&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-we-define-toxic-combinations\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;You could define a &amp;quot;toxic combination&amp;quot; in a few different ways, but here is a practical one based on how we look at our own datasets. Most web attacks eventually scale through automation; once an attacker finds a viable exploit, they&amp;#39;ll usually script it into a bot to finish the job. &lt;b&gt;By looking at the intersection of bot traffic, specific application paths, request anomalies and misconfigurations, we can spot a potential breach.&lt;/b&gt; We use this framework to reason through millions of requests per second.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While point defenses like Web Application Firewalls (WAF), bot detection, and API protection have evolved to incorporate behavioral patterns and reputation signals, they still primarily focus on evaluating the risk of an individual request. In contrast, Cloudflareâs detections for &amp;quot;toxic combinations&amp;quot; shift the lens toward the broader intent, analyzing the confluence of context surrounding multiple signals to identify a brewing incident.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1OpmbSTqET3QnkdoHXJeim/882c3385ad8e172bfbec3dafffe7477e/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1936\&quot; height=\&quot;434\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Toxic combinations as contextualized detections&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That shift in perspective matters because many real incidents have no obvious exploit payload, no clean signatures, and no single event that screams âattack.â So, in what follows, we combine the following context to construct several toxic combinations:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Bot signals&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Application paths&lt;/b&gt;, especially sensitivity ones: admin, debug, metrics, search, payment flows&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Anomalies&lt;/b&gt; including: unexpected http codes, geo jumps, identity mismatch, high ID churn, rate-limit evasion (distributed IPs doing the same thing), request or success rate spikesÂ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Vulnerabilities or misconfigurations&lt;/b&gt;: missing session cookies or auth headers, predictable identifiers&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;examples-of-toxic-combinations-on-popular-application-stacks\&quot;&gt;Examples of toxic combinations on popular application stacks&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#examples-of-toxic-combinations-on-popular-application-stacks\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;We looked at a 24-hour window of Cloudflare data to see how often these patterns actually appear in popular application stacks. As shown in the table below, about 11% of the hosts we analyzed were susceptible to these combinations, skewed by vulnerable WordPress websites. Excluding WordPress sites, only 0.25% of hosts show signs of exploitable toxic combinations. While rare, they represent hosts that are vulnerable to compromise.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To make sense of the data, we broke it down into three stages of an attack:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Estimated hosts probed:&lt;/b&gt; This is the &amp;quot;wide net.&amp;quot; It counts unique hosts where we saw HTTP requests targeting specific sensitive paths (like &lt;code&gt;/wp-admin&lt;/code&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Estimated hosts filtered by toxic combination:&lt;/b&gt; Here, we narrowed the list down to the specific hosts that actually met our criteria for a toxic combination.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Estimated reachable hosts:&lt;/b&gt; Unique hosts that responded successfully to an exploit attemptâthe &amp;quot;smoking gun&amp;quot; of an attack. A simple &lt;code&gt;200 OK&lt;/code&gt; response (such as one triggered by appending &lt;code&gt;?debug=true&lt;/code&gt;) could be a false positive. We validated paths to filter out noise caused by authenticated paths that require credentials despite the 200 status code, redirects that mask the true exploit path, and origin misconfigurations that serve success codes for unreachable paths.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;In the next sections, weâll dig into the specific findings and the logic behind the combinations that drove them. The detection queries provided are necessary but not sufficient without testing for reachability; it is possible that the findings might be false positives. In some cases, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/products/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Log Explorer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; allows these queries to be executed on unsampled Cloudflare logs.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;Table 1. A templatized version of the query, executable in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/products/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Log Explorer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, is below:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;SELECT\n  clientRequestHTTPHost,\n  COUNT(*) AS request_count\nFROM\n  http_requests \nWHERE\n  timestamp &amp;gt;= &amp;#039;{{START_DATE}}&amp;#039;\n  AND timestamp &amp;lt;= &amp;#039;{{END_DATE}}&amp;#039;\n  AND edgeResponseStatus = 200\n  AND clientRequestPath LIKE &amp;#039;{{PATH_PATTERN}}&amp;#039; //e.g. &amp;#039;%/wp-admin/%&amp;#039;\n  AND NOT match( extract(clientRequestHTTPHost, &amp;#039;^[^:/]+&amp;#039;), &amp;#039;^\\\\d{1,3}(\\\\.\\\\d{1,3}){3}(:\\\\d+)?$&amp;#039;) // comment this line for Cloudflare Log Explorer\n  AND botScore &amp;lt; {{BOT_THRESHOLD}} // we used botScore &amp;lt; 30\nGROUP BY\n  clientRequestHTTPHost\nORDER BY\n  request_count DESC;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;why-is-this-serious\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Why is this serious?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#why-is-this-serious\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Publicly accessible admin panels can enable &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/bots/brute-force-attack/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;brute force attacks&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. If successful, an attacker can further compromise the host by adding it to a botnet that probes additional websites for similar vulnerability. In addition, this toxic combination can lead to:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Exploit scanning:&lt;/b&gt; Attackers identify the specific software version you&amp;#39;re running (like Tomcat or WordPress) and launch targeted exploits for known vulnerabilities (CVEs).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;User enumeration:&lt;/b&gt; Many admin panels accidentally reveal valid usernames, which helps attackers craft more convincing phishing or login attacks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-evidence-supports-it\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;What evidence supports it?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-evidence-supports-it\&quot; /admin/&lt;/b&gt;,&lt;b&gt; /administrator/&lt;/b&gt;, &lt;b&gt;/actuator/*&lt;/b&gt;,&lt;b&gt; /_search/&lt;/b&gt;,&lt;b&gt; /phpmyadmin/&lt;/b&gt;,&lt;b&gt; /manager/html/&lt;/b&gt;, and&lt;b&gt; /app/kibana/&lt;/b&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Ingredient&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Signal&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Description&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Bot activity&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Bot Score &amp;lt; 30&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Bot signatures typical of vulnerability scanners&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Anomaly&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Repeated Probing&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Unusual hits on admin endpoints&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Vulnerability&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Publicly accessible endpoint&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Successful requests to admin endpoints&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-do-i-mitigate-this-finding\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;How do I mitigate this finding?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-do-i-mitigate-this-finding\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Implement &lt;/b&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/sase/products/access/\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Zero Trust Access&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;b&gt;Â &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;If for any reason the endpoint has to remain public, implement&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/products/turnstile/\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;a challenge platform to add friction to bots&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Implement IP allowlist:&lt;/b&gt; Use your &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/wildcard-rules/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;WAF&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; or server configuration to ensure that administrative paths are only reachable from your corporate VPN or specific office IP addresses.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cloak admin paths:&lt;/b&gt; If your platform allows it, rename default admin URLs (e.g., change &lt;code&gt;/wp-admin&lt;/code&gt; to a unique, non-guessable string).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Deploy geo-blocking:&lt;/b&gt; If your administrators only operate from specific countries, block all traffic to these sensitive paths coming from outside those regions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Enforce multi-factor authentication (MFA):&lt;/b&gt; Ensure every administrative entry point requires a second factor; a password alone is not enough to stop a dedicated crawler.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;unauthenticated-public-api-endpoints-allowing-mass-data-exposure-via-predictable-identifiers\&quot;&gt;Unauthenticated public API endpoints allowing mass data exposure via predictable identifiers&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#unauthenticated-public-api-endpoints-allowing-mass-data-exposure-via-predictable-identifiers\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; Even worse, the way it identifies records (using simple, predictable ID numbers,see &lt;a href=\&quot;https://owasp.org/API-Security/editions/2023/en/0xa1-broken-object-level-authorization/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;OWASP: API1:2023- Broken Object Level Authorization&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) allows anyone to simply &amp;quot;count&amp;quot; through your database â making it much simpler for attackers to enumerate and âscrapeâ your business records, without even visiting your website directly.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;SELECT\n  uniqExact(clientRequestHTTPHost) AS unique_host_count\nFROM  http_requests\nWHERE timestamp &amp;gt;= &amp;#039;2026-02-13&amp;#039;\n  AND timestamp &amp;lt;= &amp;#039;2026-02-14&amp;#039;\n  AND edgeResponseStatus = 200\n  AND bmScore &amp;lt; 30\n  AND (\n       match(extract(clientRequestQuery, &amp;#039;(?i)(?:^|[&amp;amp;?])uid=([^&amp;amp;]+)&amp;#039;),  &amp;#039;^[0-9]{3,10}$&amp;#039;)\n    OR match(extract(clientRequestQuery, &amp;#039;(?i)(?:^|[&amp;amp;?])user=([^&amp;amp;]+)&amp;#039;), &amp;#039;^[0-9]{3,10}$&amp;#039;)\n    OR length(extract(clientRequestQuery, &amp;#039;(?i)(?:^|[&amp;amp;?])uid=([^&amp;amp;]+)&amp;#039;))  BETWEEN 3 AND 8\n    OR length(extract(clientRequestQuery, &amp;#039;(?i)(?:^|[&amp;amp;?])user=([^&amp;amp;]+)&amp;#039;)) BETWEEN 3 AND 8\n  )&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;why-is-this-serious\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Why is this serious?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#why-is-this-serious\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;This is a &amp;quot;zero-exploit&amp;quot; vulnerability, meaning an attacker doesn&amp;#39;t need to be a hacker to steal your data; they just need to change a number in a web link. This leads to:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Mass Data Exposure:&lt;/b&gt; Large-scale scraping of your entire customer dataset.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Secondary Attacks:&lt;/b&gt; Stolen data is used for targeted phishing or account takeovers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Regulatory Risk:&lt;/b&gt; Severe privacy violations (GDPR/CCPA) due to exposing sensitive PII.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Fraud:&lt;/b&gt; Competitors or malicious actors gaining insight into your business volume and customer base.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-evidence-supports-it\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;What evidence supports it?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-evidence-supports-it\&quot; 30&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;High volume of requests from a single client fingerprint iterating through different IDs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Anomaly&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;High Cardinality of tid&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;A single visitor accessing hundreds or thousands of unique resource IDs in a short window.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Anomaly&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Stable Response Size&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Consistent JSON structures and file sizes, indicating successful data retrieval for each guessed ID.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Vulnerability&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Missing Auth Signals&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Requests lack session cookies, Bearer tokens, or Authorization headers entirely.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Misconfiguration&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Predictable Identifiers&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;code&gt;tid&lt;/code&gt; parameter uses low-entropy, predictable integers (e.g., 1001, 1002, 1003).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;While the query checked for bot score and predictable identifiers, signals like high cardinality, stable response sizes and missing authentication were tested on a sample of traffic matching the query.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-do-i-mitigate-this-finding\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;How do I mitigate this finding?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-do-i-mitigate-this-finding\&quot; Immediately require a valid session or API key for the affected endpoint. Do not allow &amp;quot;Anonymous&amp;quot; access to data containing PII or business secrets.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Implement authorization (IDOR check):&lt;/b&gt; Ensure the backend checks that the authenticated user actually has permission to view the specific &lt;code&gt;tid&lt;/code&gt; they are requesting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Use UUIDs:&lt;/b&gt; Replace predictable, sequential integer IDs with long, random strings (UUIDs) to make &amp;quot;guessing&amp;quot; identifiers computationally impossible.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Deploy API Shield:&lt;/b&gt; Enable Cloudflare &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/api-abuse-detection/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;API Shield&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; with features like &lt;b&gt;Schema Validation&lt;/b&gt; (to block unexpected inputs) and &lt;b&gt;BOLA Detection&lt;/b&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;debug-parameter-probing-revealing-system-details\&quot;&gt;Debug parameter probing revealing system details&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#debug-parameter-probing-revealing-system-details\&quot; appended to web paths to reveal system details. A templatized version of the query, executable in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/products/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Log Explorer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, is below:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;SELECT\n  clientRequestHTTPHost,\n  COUNT(rayId) AS request_count\nFROM\n  http_requests\nWHERE\n  timestamp &amp;gt;= &amp;#039;{{START_TIMESTAMP}}&amp;#039;\n  AND timestamp &amp;lt; &amp;#039;{{END_TIMESTAMP}}&amp;#039;\n  AND edgeResponseStatus = 200\n  AND clientRequestQuery LIKE &amp;#039;%debug=false%&amp;#039;\n  AND botScore &amp;lt; {{BOT_THRESHOLD}}\nGROUP BY\n  clientRequestHTTPHost\nORDER BY\n  request_count DESC;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;why-is-this-serious\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Why is this serious?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#why-is-this-serious\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;While this doesn&amp;#39;t steal data instantly, it provides an attacker with a high-definition map of your internal infrastructure. This &amp;quot;reconnaissance&amp;quot; makes their next attack much more likely to succeed because they can see:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Hidden data fields:&lt;/b&gt; Sensitive internal information that isn&amp;#39;t supposed to be visible to users.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Technology stack details:&lt;/b&gt; Specific software versions and server types, allowing them to look up known vulnerabilities for those exact versions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Logic hints:&lt;/b&gt; Error messages or stack traces that explain exactly how your code works, helping them find ways to break it.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-evidence-supports-it\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;What evidence supports it?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-evidence-supports-it\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; and monitoring dashboards are visible to the entire Internet. Specifically, paths like &lt;code&gt;/actuator/metrics&lt;/code&gt; are responding to anyone who asks. A templatized version of the query, executable in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/products/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Log Explorer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, is below::&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;SELECT\n  clientRequestHTTPHost,\n  count() AS request_count\nFROM http_requests\nWHERE timestamp &amp;gt;= toDateTime(&amp;#039;{{START_DATE}}&amp;#039;)\n  AND timestamp &amp;lt;  toDateTime(&amp;#039;{{END_DATE}}&amp;#039;)\n  AND botScore &amp;lt; 30\n  AND edgeResponseStatus = 200\n  AND clientRequestPath LIKE &amp;#039;%/actuator/metrics%&amp;#039; // an example\nGROUP BY\n  clientRequestHTTPHost\nORDER BY request_count DESC&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Why is this serious?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While these endpoints don&amp;#39;t usually leak customer passwords directly, they provide the &amp;quot;blueprints&amp;quot; for a sophisticated attack. Exposure leads to:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Strategic timing:&lt;/b&gt; Attackers can monitor your CPU and memory usage in real-time to launch a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ddos/glossary/denial-of-service/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Denial of Service (DoS) attack&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; exactly when your systems are already stressed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Infrastructure mapping:&lt;/b&gt; These logs often reveal the names of internal services, dependencies, and version numbers, helping attackers find known vulnerabilities to exploit.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Exploitation chaining:&lt;/b&gt; Information about thread counts and environment hints can be used to bypass security layers or escalate privileges within your network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-evidence-supports-it\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;What evidence supports it?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-evidence-supports-it\&quot; that are intended for private observability.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Vulnerability&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Missing Auth&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;These endpoints are reachable without a session token, API key, or IP-based restriction.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-do-i-mitigate-this-finding\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;How do I mitigate this finding?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-do-i-mitigate-this-finding\&quot; Immediately create a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/wildcard-rules/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;firewall rule&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to block any external traffic requesting paths containing &lt;code&gt;/actuator/&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code&gt;/prometheus&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Bind to localhost:&lt;/b&gt; Reconfigure your application frameworks to only serve these monitoring endpoints on &lt;code&gt;localhost&lt;/code&gt; The templatized query is:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;SELECT\n  clientRequestHTTPHost,\n  count() AS request_count\nFROM http_requests\nWHERE timestamp &amp;gt;= toDateTime(&amp;#039;{{START_DATE}}&amp;#039;)\n  AND timestamp &amp;lt;  toDateTime(&amp;#039;{{END_DATE}}&amp;#039;)\n  AND botScore &amp;lt; 30\n  AND edgeResponseStatus = 200\nAND clientRequestPath like &amp;#039;%/\\_search%&amp;#039;\nAND NOT match(extract(clientRequestHTTPHost, &amp;#039;^[^:/]+&amp;#039;), &amp;#039;^\\\\d{1,3}(\\\\.\\\\d{1,3}){3}(:\\\\d+)?$&amp;#039;)\nGROUP BY\n  clientRequestHTTPHost&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;why-is-this-serious\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Why is this serious?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#why-is-this-serious\&quot; Attackers can &amp;quot;dump&amp;quot; entire indices, stealing millions of records in minutes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Internal reconnaissance:&lt;/b&gt; By viewing your &amp;quot;indices&amp;quot; (the list of what you store), attackers can identify other high-value targets within your network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Data sabotage:&lt;/b&gt; Depending on the setup, an attacker might not just read data â they could potentially modify or delete your entire search index, causing a massive service outage.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-evidence-supports-it\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;What evidence supports it?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-evidence-supports-it\&quot;
